Its easy to use, dries my hair (shoulder length) in just a few minutes and its super nice to have the alternative brushes and direct blow drying thingy (if we're being honest, i use that attachment to de-fog the bathroom mirror).<br /><br />I had read a few reviews saying it was really loud and I have to say...its not. I mean, its not whisper-quiet, but what hair dryer is? In certain positions it can be louder because you may have it closer to or directed towards your ear, but it is by no means remarkably loud.<br /><br />A few reviews also said it got too hot. Sure thing it does. Its a hair dryer. Go use a traditional dryer for 5 minutes and then try to touch the part where the hot air comes out. Being the not-so-girly gal that I am, I have little knowledge surrounding the precise use of most hair styling equipment (curling irons are my nemesis) so I'm fairly confident that if I'm able to use this and not burn myself, I'm pretty sure you'll be ok too. Obviously, touching the metal portion of the one brush will result in some discomfort...its hot metal. duh. I also find it cools off fairly quick too. By the time I'm done getting ready after drying my hair (15min tops) its cool enough to get shoved back in the drawer.<br /><br />If I had one complaint, it would be that it doesnt add any significant volume to my hair. But it gets it dry and smooth in just a few minutes, so I'm able to throw in some other product to get that volume...but as was mentioned before, my hair is difficult and nothing really gives it much volume. My 'goal' in buying this was to have a way to quickly and conveniently dry my hair and this more than delivers.

  512. I have been using hot air brushes to curl my damp hair for years, and my latest one finally bit the dust. After reading the reviews, I thought this would be a good replacement, and I really wanted to like it. It turned out to be a disappointment, however.<br /><br />With other hot air brushes, direct contact with the hot element is what has made my hair soft, shiny, and dry. The thick bristles on the tube attachments of this brush do not allow very much of your hair to touch the heating element (unless you really tug, which is not great for damp hair), so basically your hair is sitting about a centimeter away from the tourmaline ceramic element. The large tube attachment has both bristles and plastic spokes, which are different lengths, so when your hair is wrapped around the tube it is almost in a square shape as it dries, resulting in uneven proximity to the heated element.<br /><br />There is no button that loosens the tube attachment so you can quickly and smoothly unfurl your hair, so you have to twirl the whole (rather large and bulky) body of the machine to get your hair out. This tired my wrist out before I was halfway done doing my hair, and the rushed job on the second half shows.<br /><br />As other reviewers mentioned, it is very easy to accidentally move the power/temp button with your fingers as you do your hair, resulting in a few surprise temperature changes and turnings-off.<br /><br />I did the best I could with it so I could leave the house to buy another dryer. My hair doesn't look terrible, but the texture is more frizzy and less silky/shiny than it was with other hot air brushes, the curls are not as tight, my scalp hurts from trying to move my hair through the VERY dense bristles on the attachment, and my wrists hurt from constantly twirling the entire apparatus to uncurl my hair.<br /><br />I gave it two stars rather than one because my hair is dry and basically presentable--but it does not look or feel as nice as it normally does, andrequired too much struggle for such a lackluster result.<br /><br />Like I said, I really wanted to like it, but I would suggest spending a few extra dollars on whatever model has features that mitigate the shortcomings of this hot air dryer.
